    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <meta name="journal_id" content="41438"/>

    <meta name="dc.title" content="The de novo genome assembly of Tapiscia sinensis and the transcriptomic and developmental bases of androdioecy"/>

    <meta name="dc.source" content="Horticulture Research 2020 7:1"/>

    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html"/>

    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Nature Publishing Group"/>

    <meta name="dc.date" content="2020-12-01"/>

    <meta name="dc.type" content="OriginalPaper"/>

    <meta name="dc.language" content="En"/>

    <meta name="dc.copyright" content="2020 The Author(s)"/>

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com"/>

    <meta name="dc.description" content="Tapiscia sinensis (Tapisciaceae) possesses an unusual androdioecious breeding system that has attracted considerable interest from evolutionary biologists. Key aspects of T. sinensis biology, including its biogeography, genomics, and sex-linked genes, are unknown. Here, we report the first de novo assembly of the genome of T. sinensis. The genome size was 410&#8201;Mb, with 22,251 predicted genes. Based on whole-genome resequencing of 55 trees from 10 locations, an analysis of population genetic structure indicated that T. sinensis has fragmented into five lineages, with low intrapopulation genetic diversity and little gene flow among populations. By comparing whole-genome scans of male versus hermaphroditic pools, we identified 303 candidate sex-linked genes, 79 of which (25.9%) were located on scaffold 25. A 24-kb region was absent in hermaphroditic individuals, and five genes in that region, TsF-box4, TsF-box10, TsF-box13, TsSUT1, and TsSUT4, showed expression differences between mature male and hermaphroditic flowers. The results of this study shed light on the breeding system evolution and conservation genetics of the Tapisciaceae."/>

Key aspects of T. sinensis biology, including its biogeography, genomics, and sex-linked genes, are unknown. Here, we report the first de novo assembly of the genome of T. sinensis. The genome size was 410&#8201;Mb, with 22,251 predicted genes. Based on whole-genome resequencing of 55 trees from 10 locations, an analysis of population genetic structure indicated that T. sinensis has fragmented into five lineages, with low intrapopulation genetic diversity and little gene flow among populations. The results of this study shed light on the breeding system evolution and conservation genetics of the Tapisciaceae."/>

            <div class="c-article-body">
                <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p><i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> (Tapisciaceae) possesses an unusual androdioecious breeding system that has attracted considerable interest from evolutionary biologists. Key aspects of <i>T. sinensis</i> biology, including its biogeography, genomics, and sex-linked genes, are unknown. Here, we report the first de novo assembly of the genome of <i>T. sinensis</i>. The genome size was 410âMb, with 22,251 predicted genes. Based on whole-genome resequencing of 55 trees from 10 locations, an analysis of population genetic structure indicated that <i>T. sinensis</i> has fragmented into five lineages, with low intrapopulation genetic diversity and little gene flow among populations. By comparing whole-genome scans of male versus hermaphroditic pools, we identified 303 candidate sex-linked genes, 79 of which (25.9%) were located on scaffold 25. A 24-kb region was absent in hermaphroditic individuals, and five genes in that region, <i>TsF-box4</i>, <i>TsF-box10</i>, <i>TsF-box13</i>, <i>TsSUT1</i>, and <i>TsSUT4</i>, showed expression differences between mature male and hermaphroditic flowers. The results of this study shed light on the breeding system evolution and conservation genetics of the Tapisciaceae.</p></div></div></section>

                </noscript>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p><i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> Oliv. (Tapisciaceae), is a woody, perennial, androdioecious species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, W. Z., Kang, H. Q., Zheng, H. C. &amp; Feng, Y. Z. An investigation on the sexual reproductive cycle in Tapiscia sinensis. J. Syst. Evol. 46, 175â182 (2008)." href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d27579e478">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhou, X. J., Ma, L. &amp; Liu, W. Z. Functional androdioecy in the rare endemic tree Tapiscia sinensis. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 180, 504â514 (2016)." href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d27579e478_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, K. et al. Carbohydrate metabolism and gene regulation during anther development in an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Ann. Bot. 120, 967â977 (2017)." href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d27579e478_2">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e478_3">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Abnormal 1 tapetum development in hermaphrodites of an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Tree Physiol. 40, 108â118 (2019)." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d27579e478_4">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Anatomy and RNA-Seq reveal important gene pathways regulating sex differentiation in a functionally Androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. BMC Plant Biol. 19, 554 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d27579e481">6</a></sup>. Androdioecy is a rare breeding system in which populations consist of only male and hermaphroditic individuals<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Pannell, J. R. The evolution and maintenance of androdioecy. Annu. Rev. Ecol. Evol. S. 33, 397â425 (2002)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d27579e485">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Choudhury, B. I., Khan, M. L. &amp; Dayanandan, S. Functional androdioecy in critically endangered Gymnocladus assamicus (Leguminosae) in the eastern Himalayan region of northeast India. PLoS ONE 9, e87287 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d27579e488">8</a></sup>. Hermaphroditic individuals have both male and female functions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Akimoto, J., Fukuhara, T. &amp; Kikuzawa, K. Sex ratios and genetic variation in a functionally androdioecious species, Schizopepon bryoniaefolius (Cucurbitaceae). Am. J. Bot. 86, 880â886 (1999)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d27579e492">9</a></sup>. Functional androdioecy is found in less than 0.005% of angiosperms<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Vernet, P. et al. Evidence for the long-term maintenance of a rare self-incompatibility system in Oleaceae. N. Phytol. 210, 1408â1417 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d27579e496">10</a></sup>, including <i>Mercurialis annua</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Liston, A., Rieseberg, L. H. &amp; Elias, T. S. Functional androdioecy in the flowering plant Datisca glomerata. Nature 343, 641â642 (1990)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d27579e503">11</a></sup>, <i>Datisca glomerata</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Liston, A., Rieseberg, L. H. &amp; Elias, T. S. Functional androdioecy in the flowering plant Datisca glomerata. Nature 343, 641â642 (1990)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d27579e509">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Wolf, D. E., Satkoski, J. A., White, K. &amp; Rieseberg, L. H. Sex determination in the androdioecious plant Datisca glomerata and its dioecious sister species D. cannabina. Genetics 159, 1243â1257 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d27579e512">12</a></sup>, <i>Schizopepon bryoniaefolius</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Akimoto, J., Fukuhara, T. &amp; Kikuzawa, K. L. &amp; Beverly, J. R. Do inbreeding depression and relative male fitness explain the maintenance of androdioecy in white mangrove, Laguncularia racemosa (Combretaceae)? N. Assessment of genetic diversity among androdioecious ancient Osmanthus fragrans trees by SSR markers. Plant Syst. Ecol. 61, 179â185 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d27579e534">15</a></sup>. <i>T. sinensis</i> has research value as a model for the study of the evolution and maintenance of androdioecy<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Liu, W. Z., Kang, H. Q., Zheng, H. C. &amp; Feng, Y. Z. An investigation on the sexual reproductive cycle in Tapiscia sinensis. J. Syst. Evol. 46, 175â182 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d27579e541">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Zhou, X. J., Ma, L. &amp; Liu, W. Z. Functional androdioecy in the rare endemic tree Tapiscia sinensis. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 180, 504â514 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d27579e544">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e547">4</a></sup>. In <i>T. sinensis</i>, floral buds on hermaphroditic individuals initiate differentiation in May, flower in late June, and are fertilized in early July<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Liu, W. Z., Kang, H. Q., Zheng, H. C. &amp; Feng, Y. Z. An investigation on the sexual reproductive cycle in Tapiscia sinensis. J. Syst. Evol. 46, 175â182 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d27579e554">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Zhou, X. J., Ma, L. &amp; Liu, W. Z. Functional androdioecy in the rare endemic tree Tapiscia sinensis. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 180, 504â514 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d27579e557">2</a></sup>. After 9 months of quiescence, young fruits resume development in April, reaching maturity in September. Thus, the flower and fruit development of <i>T</i>. <i>sinensis</i> lasts 17 months<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Liu, W. Z., Kang, H. Q., Zheng, H. C. &amp; Feng, Y. Z. An investigation on the sexual reproductive cycle in Tapiscia sinensis. J. Syst. Evol. 46, 175â182 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d27579e568">1</a></sup>, a phenomenon more common in gymnosperms<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="APG II. An update of the Angiosperm Phylogeny Group classification for the orders and families of flowering plants: APG II. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 141, 399â436 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d27579e572">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Tang, Z. X. et al. Investigation on sexual flowering and fruiting periods in Torreya garandis. J. Syst. Evol. 24, 447â453 (1986)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d27579e575">17</a></sup>. Other angiosperms with long flower and fruit development<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Chen, Z. D., Xing, S. P., Liang, H. X. &amp; Lu, A. M. Morphogenesis of female reproductive organs in Carpinus turczaninowii and Ostryopsis davidiana (Betulaceae). Acta Bot. Sin. 43, 1110â1114 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d27579e579">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Liu, X. &amp; Yang, C. Temporal characteristics of developmental cycles of female and male flowers in Betula platyphylla in northeastern China. Sci. Silvae Sin. 42, 28â42 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d27579e582">19</a></sup> include <i>Carpinus turczaninowii</i>, <i>Ostryopsis davidiana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Chen, Z. D., Xing, S. P., Liang, H. X. &amp; Lu, A. M. Morphogenesis of female reproductive organs in Carpinus turczaninowii and Ostryopsis davidiana (Betulaceae). Acta Bot. Sin. 43, 1110â1114 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d27579e592">18</a></sup>, <i>Betula platyphylla</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Liu, X. &amp; Yang, C. Temporal characteristics of developmental cycles of female and male flowers in Betula platyphylla in northeastern China. Sci. Silvae Sin. 42, 28â42 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d27579e598">19</a></sup>, and trees in section <i>Lobatae</i> of <i>Quercus</i>.</p><p><i>Tapiscia</i> was formerly widespread in the Northern Hemisphere. More than ten fossil species are described among the Eocene flora (~60 million years ago, Ma) of China<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhang, P. et al. Abh. 26, 199â238 (1976)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d27579e617">21</a></sup>, Germany<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="RÃ¼ffle, L. et al. Megafossil flora from the Genesee locality, Alberta, Canada. Palaeontogr. Abt. B. 147, 1â41 (1974)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d27579e629">23</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig1">1a</a>). Currently, the genus comprises a single species, <i>T. sinensis</i>, which is distributed in central, subtropical mountains of China, south of the Yangtze River between elevations of 250 and 2200âm, and in northern Vietnam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Liu, W. Z., Kang, H. Q., Zheng, H. C. &amp; Feng, Y. Z. An investigation on the sexual reproductive cycle in Tapiscia sinensis. J. Syst. Evol. 46, 175â182 (2008)." href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d27579e640">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhou, X. J., Ma, L. &amp; Liu, W. Z. Functional androdioecy in the rare endemic tree Tapiscia sinensis. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 180, 504â514 (2016)." href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d27579e640_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, K. et al. Carbohydrate metabolism and gene regulation during anther development in an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Ann. Bot. 120, 967â977 (2017)." href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d27579e640_2">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e640_3">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Abnormal 1 tapetum development in hermaphrodites of an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Tree Physiol. 40, 108â118 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d27579e643">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Eppley, S. M. &amp; John, R. P. Density-dependent self-fertilization and male versus hermaphrodite siring success in an androdioecious plant. Evolution 61, 2349â2359 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d27579e646">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Zhang, J. et al. Phylogeography and genetic structure of a tertiary relict tree species, Tapiscia sinensis (Tapisciaceae): implications for conservation. Ann. Bot. 116, 727â737 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d27579e649">25</a></sup>. Due to deforestation and reclamation, natural populations of <i>T. sinensis</i> are rare [International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) Red List]; it grows only in small, scattered, disjunct sites, mostly at higher elevations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhang, J. et al. Phylogeography and genetic structure of a tertiary relict tree species, Tapiscia sinensis (Tapisciaceae): implications for conservation. Ann. Bot. 116, 727â737 (2015)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d27579e656">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xie, C. P. A Review of research advances in rare and endangered plant Tapiscia sinensis. Subtropical Plant Sci. 35, 71â74 (2006)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d27579e656_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Characterization of the complete chloroplast genome sequence of Tapiscia sinensis (Tapisciaceae). Conserv. Genet. Resour. 10, 765â768 (2018)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d27579e656_2">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Zhou, X. J. et al. De novo characterization of flower bud transcriptomes and the development of EST-SSR markers for the endangered tree Tapiscia sinensis. Int. J. Mol. Sci. 16, 12855â12870 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d27579e659">28</a></sup>. The phylogenetic position of <i>T. sinensis</i> makes it an important species for understanding angiosperm evolution. In addition, this tree species has great value in Chinese traditional medicine and in landscape horticulture<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Zhou, X. J., Ma, L. &amp; Liu, W. Z. Functional androdioecy in the rare endemic tree Tapiscia sinensis. Bot. J. Linn. Soc. 180, 504â514 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d27579e667">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Zhang, J. et al. Phylogeography and genetic structure of a tertiary relict tree species, Tapiscia sinensis (Tapisciaceae): implications for conservation. Ann. Bot. 116, 727â737 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d27579e670">25</a></sup>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Comparative analysis of the Tapiscia sinensis genome with the genomes of other plant species."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1: Comparative analysis of the <i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> genome with the genomes of other plant species.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp"
