Glycine-rich proteins as structural components of plant cell walls. Cell Mol. Life Sci. 58, 1430â1441 (2001)." href="#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2883_1">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Condit, C. M. &amp; Richard, B. M. A gene encoding a novel glycine-rich structural protein of petunia. We further showed that the <i>TsGRP1.8</i> gene was highly expressed during fruit quiescence (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig5">5d</a>). The <i>GRP1.8</i> gene is part of a repair system during the stretching phase of protoxylem development<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Ringli, C., Keller, B. &amp; Ryser, U. Glycine-rich proteins as structural components of plant cell walls. Cell Mol. Life Sci. 58, 1430â1441 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2909">53</a></sup> and insolubilized within the cell wall later in development<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Condit, C. M. &amp; Richard, B. M. A gene encoding a novel glycine-rich structural protein of petunia. Nature 323, 178 (1986)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2913">54</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig5">5</a> and Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM1">17</a>). It is possible that <i>TsGRP1.8</i> plays a role in increasing the cell wall thickness or fruit stability to survive cold temperatures during quiescence (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig5">5b, d</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Ringli, C., Keller, B. &amp; Ryser, U. Glycine-rich proteins as structural components of plant cell walls. Cell Mol. Life Sci. 58, 1430â1441 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2930">55</a></sup>.</p><p>The pollen of bisexual flowers of <i>T. sinensis</i> is round and unlike that of male flowers, a phenomenon also observed in <i>Tetracera oblongata</i>, which is functionally dioecious<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Charlesworth, D. Androdioecy and the evolution of dioecy. Biol. J. Linn. Soc. 22, 333â348 (1984)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2943">56</a></sup>. This may indicate that pollen of hermaphroditic plants of <i>T. sinensis</i> is nonfunctional, a possibility suggested by Charlesworth (1984) as likely based on theoretical considerations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Lloyd, D. G. The maintenance of gynodioecy and androdioecy in angiosperms. Genetica 45, 325â339 (1975)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2950">57</a></sup>. Charlesworth<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Symon, D. E. Sex forms in Solanum (Solanaceae) and the role of pollen collecting insects. In Linnean Society symposium series 385â397 (1979)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2955">58</a></sup> also considered the 1:1 ratio of male to fruitful plants that we observed to be evidence that hermaphroditic plants were male sterile. We did not observe whether hermaphrodite pollen was fertile but did observe that hermaphrodite pollen can be shed onto adjacent stigmas, an event that would lead to inbreeding unless there is a self-incompatibility system, which we did see evidence of in nine <i>F-box</i> genes (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM1">15</a>). Charlesworth agreed with Sobrevila and Arroyo (1982), who speculated that in <i>Matayaba tovarensis</i>, dioecy evolved from self-incompatibility in hermaphrodites<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Bovrevila, C. &amp; Arroyo, M. T. K. Breeding systems in a montane cloud forest in Venezuela. Plant Syst. Evol. 140, 19â37 (1982)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d27579e2968">59</a></sup>. Charlesworth (1984) further stated that âwhen pollen is actually produced in females, but is nonfunctional, a role for inbreeding avoidance seems particularly clearâ, as sterile pollen can still attract pollinators. We did not record whether <i>T. sinensis</i> produces nectar as a reward, but <i>TsSUT3</i> was expressed in flowers but not fruit, so it could be related to nectar production (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM1">14</a> and Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig4">4i</a>). We also observed that the expression of some <i>SUT</i> genes was consistent with a role in fruit development, which of course only happens in hermaphroditic plants. It makes sense that sucrose transporters would be needed for fruit development.</p><p>In conclusion, the genome assembly of <i>T. sinensis</i> provides a reference for future genetic, genomic and evolutionary studies in <i>Tapiscia</i> and its relatives. <i>T. sinensis</i> was fragmented into five lineages based on whole-genome resequencing data from 10 populations and 55 individuals. A 24-kb region located on scaffold 25 was absent in the hermaphroditic individuals. It was rich in candidate sex-linked genes, e.g., <i>TsRPL10A9</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Ferreyra, M. L. F., Casadevall, R., Luciani, M. D., Pezza, A. &amp; Casati, P. New evidence for differential roles of l10 ribosomal proteins from Arabidopsis. Plant Physiol. 163, 378â391 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3003">52</a></sup>. We further identified eight <i>F-box</i> genes, six <i>LEA</i> genes, four <i>SUT</i> genes, and one <i>GRP</i> gene that are involved in sugar metabolism in fruit, overwintering fruit development, and flower development<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lai, Z. et al. An F-box gene linked to the self-incompatibility (S) locus of Antirrhinum is expressed specifically in pollen and tapetum. Plant Mol. Biol. 50, 29â42 (2002)." href="#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3020">42</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Nasrallah, M. E., Pei, L. &amp; June, B. N. Generation of self-incompatible Arabidopsis thaliana by transfer of two S locus genes from A. lyrata. Science 297, 247â249 (2002)." href="#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3020_1">43</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Jane, M. et al. Expression of a Self-lncompatibility Glycoprotein (S2-Ribonuclease) from Nicotiana alata in Transgenic Nicotiana tabacum. Plant Cell 4, 1063â1074 (1992)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3023">44</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ringli, C., Keller, B. &amp; Ryser, U. Glycine-rich proteins as structural components of plant cell walls. Cell Mol. Life Sci. 58, 1430â1441 (2001)." href="#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Condit, C. M. &amp; Richard, B. M. A gene encoding a novel glycine-rich structural protein of petunia. Nature 323, 178 (1986)." href="#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_1">54</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ringli, C., Keller, B. &amp; Ryser, U. Glycine-rich proteins as structural components of plant cell walls. Cell Mol. Life Sci. 58, 1430â1441 (2001)." href="#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_2">55</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Charlesworth, D. Androdioecy and the evolution of dioecy. Biol. J. Linn. Soc. 22, 333â348 (1984)." href="#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_3">56</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lloyd, D. G. The maintenance of gynodioecy and androdioecy in angiosperms. Genetica 45, 325â339 (1975)." href="#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_4">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Symon, D. E. Sex forms in Solanum (Solanaceae) and the role of pollen collecting insects. In Linnean Society symposium series 385â397 (1979)." href="#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_5">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bovrevila, C. &amp; Arroyo, M. T. K. Breeding systems in a montane cloud forest in Venezuela. Plant Syst. Evol. 140, 19â37 (1982)." href="#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_6">59</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Gao, J. &amp; Ting, L. Functional characterization of the late embryogenesis abundant (LEA) protein gene family from Pinus tabuliformis (Pinaceae) in Escherichia coli. Sci. Rep. 6, 19467 (2016)." href="#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_7">60</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ting, L., Gao, J. &amp; Zeng, Q. Y. Genome-wide analysis of the LEA (late embryogenesis abundant) protein gene family in Populus trichocarpa. Tree Genet. Genomes 9, 253â264 (2013)." href="#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3026_8">61</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Bai, Y. Q. &amp; Yang, Q. C. Study of late embriogenesis abundant protein. Biotechnol. Bull. 9, 1â7 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3029">62</a></sup>, potentially indicating that these genes play a role in regulating flower development and fruit quiescence during winter in <i>T. sinensis</i>. These genes may be of use for <i>T. sinensis</i> breeding or for further identification of genomic regions affecting sex determination. Finally, the identification of sex-linked genes in <i>T. sinensis</i> will inform studies on the evolution of androdioecy, sex-linked gene functional analysis, plant sexual development, and fruit development.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec13" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec13-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec13">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec13-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Tree samples</h3><p>In 2016, we collected leaf samples from a single individual of the androdioecious tree <i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> (wild male individual) growing in the Qinling Mountains, Shaanxi Province, China (E108Â°35â05.60â, N33Â°31â22.70â). High-quality genomic DNA was extracted from fresh leaf tissues using the Qiagen DNeasy Plant Mini Kit (Qiagen, Dusseldorf, Germany). In 2016, shoots were collected from 55 trees representing 10 wild populations of <i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> in seven Chinese provinces (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">18</a>). These 10 populations represented most of the geographic distribution of this endangered, woody tree species (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig2">2</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Transcriptome sample preparation and sequencing</h3><p>Five tissues (fruits, leaves, stems, roots, and male flowers) were collected from a single male tree of <i>T. sinensis</i> (located in the Qinling Mountains, Shaanxi Province, China). We also collected hermaphroditic flowers from a hermaphroditic tree growing in the Qinling Mountains (E 108Â°35â, N 33Â°31â). RNA was extracted from these materials with TRI reagent. The RNA-seq data of six tissues were used to make libraries using the TruSeqÂ® RNA Sample Preparation protocol for the Illumina HiSeq 4000 platform. Transcriptomes of 18 independent samples of tissues (four male flowers, six hermaphroditic flowers, and eight fruits) were evaluated for levels of expression using genes identified in <i>T. sinensis</i> (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">24</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Library preparation</h3><p>For Illumina sequencing (HiSeq 4000 platform), we used a paired-end library with an insert size of 350âbp. Paired-end 10X Genomics genome libraries with insert sizes of 50â100âkb were constructed using the Illumina NovaSeq platform. Long reads of 20âkb DNA inserts were constructed for PacBio single-molecule real-time sequencing to assist in genome assembly.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Genome de novo assembly</h3><p>Before sequence assembly, âdalignerâ was executed by the main script of the FALCON assembler to correct errors in the PacBio long reads and to generate consensus sequences<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Chin, C. S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050â1056 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3101">63</a></sup>. After error correction, the consensus sequences achieved accuracies up to 99.999%. Then, FALCON identified the overlaps between all pairs of the preassembled error-corrected reads. The read overlaps were used to construct a directed string graph following Myersâ algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Myers, E. W. The fragment assembly string graph. Bioinformatics 21, 79â85 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3105">64</a></sup>. Contigs were constructed by finding the paths from the string graph (falcon_sense_optionâ=â--output_multi --min_idt 0.70 --min_cov 3 --max_n_read 200 --n_core 10; overlap_filtering_settingâ=â--max_diff 100 --max_cov 100 --min_cov 3 --n_core 24)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Myers, E. W. The fragment assembly string graph. Bioinformatics 21, 79â85 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3109">64</a></sup>. Error correction of the preceding assembly was performed using the PacBio âarrowâ consensusâcalling algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Lin, H. H., Liao, Y. C. &amp; Dutilh, B. E. Evaluation and validation of assembling corrected PacBio long reads for microbial genome completion via hybrid approaches. PLoS ONE 10, e0144305 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3113">65</a></sup>. Illumina reads were error-corrected with Pilon<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3117">66</a></sup>. FragScaff software was used to extend 10X Genomics scaffolds as follows: Linked reads generated using the 10X Genomics library were aligned to the consensus sequence of the PacBio assembly to obtain superscaffolds using BOWTIE v2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nat. Methods 9, 357â359 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3122">67</a></sup>. As the length of the consensus sequence increases, fewer linked reads supporting connections are required. The consensus sequence with linked-read support was used for the subsequent assembly. The FragScaff parameters were â-fs1 â-m 3000 -q 30 -E 30000 -o 60000â -fs2 â-C 5â -fs3 â-j 1 -u 3ââ<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Adey, A. et al. In vitro, long-range sequence information for de novo genome assembly via transposase contiguity. Genome Res 24, 2041â2049 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3126">68</a></sup>. We also evaluated the completeness and accuracy of the genome assembly using Bench Marking Universal Single-copy Orthologs (BUSCO) version 4.0.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="SimÃ£o, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3130">69</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Repeat annotation</h3><p>We identified the repeat sequences in the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome using LTR_FINDER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 53, W265âW268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3146">70</a></sup>, PILER-DF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3150">71</a></sup>, RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. 2005. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 1, 351â358 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3154">72</a></sup>, and MITE-Hunter<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Han, Y. &amp; Wessler, S. R. MITE-Hunter: a program for discovering miniature inverted-repeat transposable elements from genomic sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 38, e199 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3158">73</a></sup>. The Repbase database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Bao, W. D., Kojima, K. K. &amp; Kohany, O. Repbase Update, a database of repetitive elements in eukaryotic genomes. Mob. DNA 6, 11 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3163">74</a></sup> was combined to construct a nonredundant repeat sequence library of the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome. Tandem Repeats Finder was used to identify tandem repeat sequences in the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573â580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3173">75</a></sup>. MISA software was used to identify the simple sequence repeats (SSRs), with thresholds of ten repeat units for mononucleotide SSRs and five repeat units for di-, tri-, tetra-, penta-, and hexanucleotide SSRs.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Gene prediction and annotation</h3><p>To predict genes in the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome, we used two methods: homology-based prediction with BLAST (E-valueââ¤â1e<sup>â5</sup>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Johnson, M. et al. NCBI BLAST: a better web interface. Nucleic Acids Res. 36, W5âW9 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3190">76</a></sup> and GeneWise (version 2.4.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Birney, E., Michele, C. &amp; Richard, D. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3194">77</a></sup> and ab initio prediction with Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Stanke, M. et al. AUGUSTUS: ab initio prediction of alternative transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, 435â439 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3198">78</a></sup> and GlimmerHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Majoros, W. H., Mihaela, P. &amp; Steven, L. S. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878â2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3203">79</a></sup>. We predicted the gene structure of the corresponding genomic regions using BLAST hits through GeneWise (version 2.4.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Birney, E., Michele, C. &amp; Richard, D. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3207">77</a></sup>. Protein sequences were downloaded from the NCBI to perform homology predictions. RNA-seq data derived from six tissues (fruit, leaf, stem, root, male flower, and hermaphroditic flower) were assembled using Trinity. We generated gene models using Evidence Modeler (EVM)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3211">80</a></sup>. UTR and alternative splicing variation were predicted from gene models using PASA2 software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="RodrÃ­guez, F. A. et al. Novel and recurrent COL7A1 mutations in Chilean patients with dystrophic epidermolysis bullosa. J. Dermatol. Sci. 65, 149â152 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3215">81</a></sup>.</p><p>We performed functional annotation using BLASTP with an E-value cutoff of 1e<sup>â5</sup>. Protein-coding genes were identified with searches against SwissProt and TrEMBL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Bairoch, A. &amp; Rolf, A. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 45â48 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3224">82</a></sup>. We annotated conserved protein domains using the InterPro (version 5.16)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Mulder, N. &amp; Apweiler, R. Interpro and InterProScan: tools for protein sequence classification and comparison. Methods Mol. Biol. 396, 59â70 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3228">83</a></sup> and Pfam (v 3.0) databases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Bateman, A. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, D138âD141 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3232">84</a></sup>. We predicted the biological pathways in the KEGG database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Kanehisa, M. &amp; Susumu, G. KEGG: kyoto encyclopedia of genes and genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 27â30 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3236">85</a></sup> using BLAST with an E-value cut-off of 1e<sup>â05</sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Comparative analysis of <i>T. sinensis</i> genome evolution</h3><p>We performed global gene family classification of 17 plant genomes, including those of <i>M. notabilis</i>, <i>Z. jujuba</i>, <i>P. persica</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>J. regia</i>, <i>J. curcas</i>, <i>G. max</i>, <i>G. raimondii</i>, <i>T. cacao</i>, <i>F. schinensis</i>, <i>P. trichocarpa</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i>, <i>C. papaya</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>O. europaea</i>, and <i>C. sinensis</i>, based on whole protein-coding gene repertoires. We performed gene pair searches within these 17 plant genomes using BLASTP. We clustered gene families from these plant species using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C. J. &amp; Roos, D. S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178â2189 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3309">86</a></sup> with the parameter â-inflation 1.5â.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Phylogenetic tree reconstruction</h3><p>We first generated a multiple sequence alignment with default parameters through MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Bateman, A. et al. The Pfam protein families database. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, D138âD141 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3321">84</a></sup>. We used ProtTest<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Abascal, F., Zardoya, R. &amp; Posada, D. ProtTest: selection of best-fit models of protein evolution. Bioinformatics 21, 2104â2105 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3325">87</a></sup> to select the best substitution models, and the JTTâ+âIâ+âGâ+âF model was selected as the best-fitting model. Then, we constructed a maximum likelihood (ML) phylogenetic tree based on 509 familiesâ genes using RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML-VI-HPC: maximum likelihood-based phylogenetic analyses with thousands of taxa and mixed models. Bioinformatics 22, 2688â2690 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3329">88</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Species divergence time estimation</h3><p>We estimated the divergence times for 18 species using MCMCTree in PAML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3341">89</a></sup> with the âcorrelated molecular clockâ and âJC69â models. We applied a total of five fossil calibration points for the estimation of divergence times: <i>O. sativa</i> and <i>S. lycopersicum</i> divergence time (115â308 million years ago), <i>V. vinifera</i> and <i>G. max</i> divergence time (107â135 million years ago), <i>V. vinifera</i> and <i>A. thaliana</i> divergence time (107â135 million years ago), <i>J. regia</i> and <i>P. trichocarpa</i> divergence time (101â131 million years ago), and <i>P. trichocarpa</i> and <i>A. thaliana</i> divergence time (98â117 million years ago) (<a href="http://www.timetree.org/">http://www.timetree.org/</a>) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#Fig1">1</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Gene family expansion and contraction</h3><p>CAFÃ 2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Bie, T. D., Cristianini, N., Demuth, J. P. &amp; Hahn, M. W. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269â1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3395">90</a></sup> (Computational Analysis of gene Family Evolution) software was used to assess the expansion and contraction of orthologous gene families among the 18 plant genomes based on a phylogenetic tree.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Whole-genome duplication analysis</h3><p>We identified syntenic blocks in the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome using MCScanX with a BLASTP E-value &lt;â1e<sup>â7</sup>. We calculated the 4DTv distance for each gene pair in a syntenic block to identify putative whole-genome duplication events in <i>T. sinensis</i>. The synonymous substitution rate (Ks) was calculated using the YN model in KaKs_Calculator v2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Wang, D., Zhang, Y., Zhang, Z., Zhu, J. &amp; Yu, J. KaKs_Calculator 2.0: a toolkit incorporating gamma-series methods and sliding window strategies. Genom. Proteom. Bioinf. 8, 77â80 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3416">91</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Transcriptome library and gene expression analysis</h3><p>Transcriptomes (<i>N</i>â=â18) were mapped to the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome using TopHat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Cole, T. &amp; Salzberg, P. L. S. L. TopHat: discovering splice junctions with RNA-Seq. Bioinformatics 9, 9 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3434">92</a></sup>. The expression of each gene was normalized by read counts (RPKM). We used DESeq to identify differentially expressed genes (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">26</a>). We generated the expression profiles of all differentially expressed genes using gCLUTO (<a href="http://glaros.dtc.umn.edu/gkhome/cluto/gcluto/overview">http://glaros.dtc.umn.edu/gkhome/cluto/gcluto/overview</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Alignment and variation calling from whole-genome resequencing data of 55 accessions</h3><p>We mapped the short reads to the <i>T. sinensis</i> genome using BWA with the following parameters: bwa mem -t 4 -M -R<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Li, H. &amp; Richard, D. Fast and accurate short read alignment with BurrowsâWheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3459">93</a></sup>. SAM/BAM files were evaluated to remove PCR duplicates using the Picard package with default parameters (<a href="http://broadinstitute.github.io/picard">http://broadinstitute.github.io/picard</a>). We computed the coverage and depth of sequence alignments using the DepthOfCoverage program in the Genome Analysis Toolkit<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome analysis toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297â1303 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3470">94</a></sup> (GATK) and BEDtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Ira, M. H. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841â8426 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3474">95</a></sup>, respectively (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">19</a>). We called SNPs following GATK best practices. Low-quality alignments with a mapping quality &lt;20 were filtered using SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3482">96</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Population genetic analysis</h3><p>We constructed a neighbor-joining (NJ) tree of 55 <i>T. sinensis</i> accessions using TreeBeST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Vilella, A. J. et al. EnsemblCompara GeneTrees: complete, duplication-aware phylogenetic trees in vertebrates. Genome Res. 19, 327â335 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3497">97</a></sup> and EvolView<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="He, Z. L. et al. Evolview v2: an online visualization and management tool for customized and annotated phylogenetic trees. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, W236âW241 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3501">98</a></sup>. We performed PCA using GCTA software with default settings<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Yang, J., Lee, S. H., Goddard, M. E. &amp; Visscher, P. M. GCTA: a tool for genome-wide complex trait analysis. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 88, 76â82 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3505">99</a></sup>. The top four eigenvectors of samples were plotted using the ggplot2 R package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Ginestet, C. ggplot2: elegant graphics for data analysis. J. R. Stat. Soc. 174, 245â246 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3509">100</a></sup>. We also investigated population structure using ADMIXTURE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Price, A. L. et al. Principal components analysis corrects for stratification in genome-wide association studies. Nat. Genet. 38, 904â909 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3514">101</a></sup>, wherein the maximum iteration time was set to 10,000, and the number of population groups (<i>K</i>) was varied from 1 to 10. We identified sex-linked genomic regions by comparing 26 hermaphroditic individuals and 29 male individuals for regions showing reduction of diversity (RODâ=â1âââÏ<sub>male</sub>/Ï<sub>hermaphroditic</sub>). <i>F</i><sub>ST</sub> parameters were calculated in windows of 10âkb along the entire <i>T. sinensis</i> genome (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">18</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Floral morphology and development</h3><p>Living tissues were collected from cultivated trees growing at Northwest University, Shanxi Province (N34Â°14'58.61â, E 108Â°55'39.72â). Samples were collected in June, July, August, September, January, February, March, and April. We observed and photographed the morphological features of <i>T. sinensis</i> using a stereomicroscope (OLYMPUS SZX12). We prepared paraffin sections using routine methods<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="Ruzin, S. E. Plant Microtechnique and Microscopy (Oxford University Press, New York) Vol. 198 (1999)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3547">102</a></sup>. Briefly, tissues of <i>T. sinensis</i> were dehydrated in an ethanol series (5âmin 85% ETOH, 95% ETOH, 100% ETOH, and 100% ETOH), infiltrated with xylene (20âmin 1/2 ETOHâ+âÂ½ xylene and 15âmin wash in 100% xylene two times)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3554">4</a></sup>, and embedded in paraffin for sectioning. The prepared slides were critically observed and photographed using a Nikon DS-Fil digital camera<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Abnormal 1 tapetum development in hermaphrodites of an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Tree Physiol. 40, 108â118 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3558">5</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">Gene families</h3><p>Query sequences of <i>RPL10A</i>, <i>SUT</i>, <i>LEA</i>, and <i>F-box</i> genes of <i>A. thaliana</i> were downloaded from TAIR (<a href="https://www.arabidopsis.org/browse/genefamily/index.jsp">https://www.arabidopsis.org/browse/genefamily/index.jsp</a>). Gene family size for <i>RPL10A</i>, <i>SUT</i>, <i>LEA</i>, and <i>F-box</i> gene families was determined using blastp with the default parameter<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 53, W265âW268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3605">70</a></sup>. We characterized the structure of <i>RPL10A</i>, <i>SUT</i>, <i>LEA</i>, and <i>F-box</i> genes using the online software GSDS2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Hu, B. et al. GSDS 2.0: an upgraded gene feature visualization server. Bioinformatics 31, 1296â1297 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3622">103</a></sup>. The protein domains of these four gene familiesâ members were predicted in NCBI software. The R package pheatmap was used to detect the expression pattern of these four gene families (R package)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Kolde, R. pheatmap: Pretty Heatmaps. R package version 1.0.2 ed. (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3626">104</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">PCR verification of <i>RPL10A</i> gene variations</h3><p>Total genomic DNA of <i>T. sinensis</i> was extracted using the CTAB method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3646">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Abnormal 1 tapetum development in hermaphrodites of an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Tree Physiol. 40, 108â118 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3649">5</a></sup>. We designed six <i>TsRPL10A</i> primer pairs to verify the genetic variation between male and hermaphroditic individuals (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">22</a>). The PCR protocols were as previously reported<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yang, K. et al. Carbohydrate metabolism and gene regulation during anther development in an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Ann. Bot. 120, 967â977 (2017)." href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3659">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xin, G. L. et al. Floral development in the androdioecious tree Tapiscia sinensis: implications for the evolution to androdioecy. J. Syst. Evol. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/jse.12517&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3659_1">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Ren, X. L. et al. Abnormal 1 tapetum development in hermaphrodites of an androdioecious tree, Tapiscia sinensis. Tree Physiol. 40, 108â118 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d27579e3662">5</a></sup>, using the previously mentioned primers (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00414-w#MOESM2">22</a>), and the PCR products were verified by agarose gel electrophoresis.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The raw reads of the genome and the resequencing data for 55 <i>Tapiscia sinensis</i> individuals have been deposited as a BioProject under accession PRJNA587558. The raw transcriptome data for flowers and fruits of <i>T. sinensis</i> have been deposited as a BioProject under accession PRJNA284864.</p>

W.Z.L., P.Z., X.L.R., H.W., and G.L.X. collected samples and performed experiments. W.Z.L. photographed the morphological features of <i>Tapiscia sinensis</i>. X.L.R., G.L.X., and W.Z.L. analyzed floral morphology and development. W.Z.L., P.Z., and G.L.X. assembled the genome. F.Y., P.Z., G.L.X., X.L.R., and W.Z.L. completed the genome annotation and evolutionary analyses. P.Z. and W.Z.L. wrote the paper. P.Z., K.W., F.Y., and W.Z.L. edited and revised the English writing of this paper. All authors read and approved the final paper.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding author</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
